[^2]: The reference is to the group of participants in the Baden uprising of April 1848 who emigrated to Besançon (France); later, under the name of the Besançon company and headed by Willich, they took part in the Baden-Palatinate uprising of 1849. p. 529

**[p. 252]**

INDEX OF PERIODICALS

LAlba. Giornale politico-letterario—Italian democratic daily published in Florence in 1847-49.—397 Allgemeine Oder-Zeitung—German daily published under this title in Breslau (Wroclaw) from 1846 to March 1849, organ of the opposition Catholic circles; in March 1849 it changed its trend and was renamed Neue Oder-Zeitung, and as an organ of German bourgeois democracy it appeared until 1855. In 1855 Marx was its correspondent in London.—427, 430, 440, 443, 461 Allgemeine Preussische Zeitung—see Preussischer Staats-Anzeiger

[^1]: Allgemeine Zeitung—German conservative daily founded in 1798; from 1810 to 1882 was published in Augsburg.—120, 122, 348, 412, 435, 478

[^2]: L'Ami du Peuple en 1848—French revolutionary-democratic newspaper published in Paris from February 27 to May 14, 1848, under the editorship of François Raspail.—127

[^3]: Arbeiter-Zeitung—see Zeitung des Arbeiter-Vereines zu Köln

[^4]: Der aufrichtige und wohlerfahrene Schweizer Bote—Swiss liberal journal founded in 1798 ; from 1804 was published in Aarau.—181

[^5]: Augsburger Allgemeine Zeitung—see Allgemeine Zeitung

[^6]: Basellandschaftliches Volksblatt—Swiss liberal weekly published in the canton of Basle from 1835 to 1853.—181

[^7]: Basler Intelligenzblatt—Swiss conservative newspaper published under this tide in Basle from 1845 to 1856.—120

[^8]: Berner Intelligenzblatt—Swiss daily published from 1834 to 1919; in the 1840s, organ of the reactionary circles.—247 Berner Verfassungs-Freund—Swiss moderate liberal daily published in Berne from 1836 to 1849, when it was renamed Schweizerische Bundeszeitung.—58, 179, 248, 251, 252, 253

[^9]: Berner-Zeitung—Swiss daily published in Berne from 1845 to 1894; in the 1840s, organ of the radical party, was edited by Niklaus Niggeler.—58, 117, 247, 248,





**[p. 633]**

Breslauer Zeitung—German daily founded in Breslau (Wroclaw) in 1820; repeatedly changed its political orientation; in the 1840s held liberal views; in 1848-49 campaigned against revolutionary Hungary.—347, 351, 425, 428, 440, 442, 451, 458, 460, 467, 468, 477

Bundeszeitung—see Schweizerische Bundeszeitung

Le Charivari—French republican satirical newspaper published in Paris from 1832 to 1934; ridiculed the regime of the July monarchy and in 1848 supported Cavaignac's dictatorship.—247

La Concordia—Italian liberal daily published in Turin in 1848-49 under the editorship of Giuseppe Gentille.—397

Constitutionelles Blatt aus Böhmen—daily published in German in Prague in 1848-49.—352, 410, 416, 431, 435, 451, 453, 468, 472, 473, 479

Constitutionnel Neuchâtelois—Swiss constitutional-monarchist newspaper published thrice weekly in Neuchâtel from 1831 to February 1848.—8

// Contemporaneo—Italian radical daily published in Rome from 1846; was suppressed by the Pope's decree of July 15, 1849.—397

Le Courrier Suisse—Swiss conservative newspaper published in Lausanne from 1840 to 1853.—43

[^1]: Deutsche Allgemeine Zeitung—German newspaper published under this title in Leipzig from 1843 to 1879; until the summer of 1848 was conservative but later adopted liberal views.—410

[^2]: Die Deutsche Reform. Politische Zeitung für das constitutionelle Deutschland—German constitutional-monarchist daily published in Berlin from June 20, 1848, to 1851.-198,421

[^3]: Deutsche Schnellpost für Europäische Zustände, öffentliches und sociales Leben Deutsch- lands—newspaper of the German moderate democratic emigrants in the USA published twice weekly in New York from 1843 to 1851.— 210

[^4]: Deutsche Zeitung—German daily published in Heidelberg from 1847 to October 1848, and up to 1850 in Frankfurt am Main; organ of the advocates of constitutional monarchy and unification of Germany under Prussian hegemony.—193, 287

[^5]: Düsseldorfer Zeitung—German daily published under this title in Düsseldorf from 1826 to 1926; was liberal in the 1840s.—79, 199, 200, 516

[^6]: Die Evolution. Ein politisches Wochenblatt—revolutionary-democratic workers' weekly, organ of the German refugees in Switzerland, published in Biel (Berne canton) in 1848 and 1849 under the editorship of Johann Philipp Becker; a specimen issue appeared on December 1, 1848, under the title Die Revolution.—204, 205, 250

[^7]: Frankfurter Journal—German daily published in Frankfurt am Main from 1615 to 1903; was liberal in the 1840s.—179, 342

[^8]: Frankfurter Oberpostamts-Zeitung—German newspaper published in Frankfurt am Main from 1619 to 1866; during the 1848-49 revolution was the organ of the Imperial Regent and the Imperial Government.—98, 117, 421





**[p. 634]**

Der Freie Schweizer—Swiss radical daily published in Berne in 1848 and 1849; in 1849 was renamed Schweizer Zeitung.—250

Freiheit, Brüderlichkeit, Arbeit—German newspaper, organ of the Cologne Workers' Association, published twice weekly in Cologne from October 26, 1848. From January 14, 1849, Gottschalk's supporters tried to replace it with the newspaper Freiheit, Arbeit which was disavowed by the Association's leadership. On February 8 the publication of the newspaper was resumed and it appeared until the middle of 1849.—513, 524

Gazette de Lausanne et Journal Suisse—Swiss daily founded in Lausanne in 1798, organ of the liberal-democratic party.—86

Grazer Zeitung—Austrian daily founded in Graz in 1785.—454, 461, 468

Der Gukkasten—Swiss radical humoristic weekly published in Berne from 1840 to the end of 1849 under the editorship of Jenni.— 249

L'Helvétie fédérale—see L'Helvétie

L'Helvétie. Journal politique, industriel et littéraire—Swiss radical daily published in Pruntrut from 1832 to 1850; from January to November 1849 appeared under the title L'Helvétie fédérale in Berne.—248

Janus. Jahrbücher deutscher Gesinnung, Bildung und That—German pietist yearbook published in Berlin from 1845 to 1848.—240

Journal du Valais—Swiss liberal newspaper published in Sion, Wallis (Valais) canton, from 1848 to 1857.—108

[^1]: Karlsruher Zeitung—German daily, official organ of the Grand Duchy of Baden, published in Karlsruhe from 1757.—193

[^2]: Kölnerin—see Kölnische Zeitung

[^3]: Kölnische Zeitung—German daily published under this title from 1802 to 1945; organ of the liberal bourgeoisie, exponent of anti-revolutionary trends in 1848-49, waged struggle against the Neue Rheinische Zeitung.—19, 29, 35, 79, 166, 193, 210, 254, 255, 257, 286-89, 290, 292, 294, 301, 347, 354-59, 392, 394, 398, 401, 402, 445, 453, 477, 529

[^4]: Königlich privilegirte Berlinische Zeitung von Staats- und gelehrten Sachen—German newspaper published in Berlin from 1785; in the 1840s held moderate liberal views; also known as the Vossische Zeitung after its owner.—36

[^5]: Közlöny, hivatalos lap— Hungarian daily, organ of the revolutionary Government of Hungary, published in Pest and Debreczin in 1848 and 1849 and in Szegedin from July 1849.—237, 348, 477, 479

[^6]: Kreuz-Zeitung—see Neue Preussische Zeitung

[^7]: Leipziger Zeitung—German conservative newspaper published under this title in Leipzig from 1810.—416, 453

[^8]: Der Lloyd—Austrian conservative newspaper appearing twice a day in Vienna from 1848 to 1854.—426, 471

[^9]: Moniteur du Soir—French daily published in Paris from 1831 ; organ of the supporters of the July monarchy until 1848; organ of the Bonapartists after 1848.—456





**[p. 635]**

Murter Wächter—Swiss radical newspaper published in Murten (Freiburg canton) from January 1848.—252

Napredak—Serbian newspaper published in Karlowitz (Karlovce) in 1848-49.— 353

Le National—French daily published in Paris from 1830 to 1851; organ of the moderate republicans in the 1840s.—66, 84, 124, 213, 281-83, 284

National-Zeitung—German liberal newspaper published under this title in Berlin from April 1, 1848, to 1915.—271-79, 446, 448

National-Zeitung—see Schweizerische National-Zeitung

Neue Kölnische Zeitung für Bürger, Bauern und Soldaten—German revolutionary- democratic newspaper published in Cologne from September 10, 1848, to July 14, 1849.—181

Neue Preussische Zeitung—German conservative daily, organ of the big Prussian landowners and Court circles; was published in Berlin from June 1848; known also as Kreuz-Zeitung because the heading contained a cross bearing the slogan "Forward with God for King and Fatherland!"—3, 30-34, 36, 99, 174, 222, 254, 259, 261, 265, 313, 325, 339

Neue Rheinische Zeitung. Organ der Demokratie—German daily, organ of the proletarian revolutionary democrats during the German revolution of 1848-49, published in Cologne under Marx's editorship from June 1, 1848, to May 19, 1849 (with an interval from September 27 to October 12, 1848).—14, 16, 18, 21, 39, 48, 49, 69, 70, 73, 81-83, 85, 94, 138, 142, 154, 159, 161, 168, 182, 188, 192, 210, 254, 256, 262, 268, 276, 286, 291, 304, 311-15, 323, 358, 362, 366, 371, 390, 416, 421, 422, 445, 493, 496, 501, 504, 509-10, 516, 517, 518, 521, 522, 527, 529, 530

[^1]: Neue Zürcher-Zeitung—see Zürcher-Zeitung

[^2]: The Northern Star—English weekly, central organ of the Chartists, published from 1837 to 1852, first in Leeds and, from November 1844, in London. Its founder and editor was Feargus O'Connor, George Harney being one of its editors. Engels contributed to the paper from 1843 to 1850.— 397

[^3]: Nouvelliste Vaudois—Swiss cantonal newspaper founded in 1798 and published in Lausanne until 1914; in the 1840s adhered to radical views.—43, 58, 248

[^4]: Oppelner Kreisblatt—weekly newspaper of the authorities in Oppeln (Silesia), published from 1840.—269

[^5]: Österreichischer Correspondent—daily organ of the Austrian Government, published under this title in Vienna in 1848 and 1849 (from November 1848 to April 1849 in Olmütz).—426 Pesther Courier—organ of the Austrian administration in Pest in 1848-49.—479

[^6]: Le Peuple. Journal de la République démocratique et sociale—French social-reformist newspaper published in Paris in 1848-50; from April 1848 it was called Le Représentant du Peuple, from September 1848 to June 13, 1849, Le Peuple and later La Voix du peuple and Le Peuple de 1850; its editor was Pierre Joseph Proudhon.—123, 128, 129, 130, 132





**[p. 636]**

La Presse—French daily published in Paris from 1836; in the 1840s expressed the interests of the circles opposed to the July monarchy; it was the organ of the moderate republicans in 1848-49, and later a Bonapartist newspaper. Emile Girardin was its editor from 1836 to 1857.—23

Preussischer Staats-Anzeiger—newspaper founded in Berlin in 1819; under this title was published from May 1848 to July 1851 as an official organ of the Prussian Government.—36, 106, 133, 19Ö, 240, 379

La Réforme—daily organ of the French republican democrats and petty-bourgeois socialists published in Paris from 1843 to 1850. Engels published several articles in it from October 1847 to October 1848.—123-24, 127, 129, 397

Le Représentant du Peuple—see Le Peuple

Le Républicain Neuchâtelois—Swiss liberal-republican newspaper published from March 1848 to October 1849 in La Chaux-de-Fonds and from November 1849 to 1856 in Neuchâtel.—8

La République—French daily, organ of the radical republicans, published in Paris from February 1848 to December 1851.—397

Die Revolution—see Die Evolution

La Révolution démocratique et sociale—French daily, organ of the democratic republicans, published in Paris from November 1848 to June 1849 under the editorship of Charles Delescluze.—123, 124-25, 127, 397

[^1]: Revue de Genève et Journal Suisse— Swiss radical newspaper published in Geneva from 1842 and edited by Jean Jacob Fazy; appeared under this title until 1861, when it merged with La Nation Suisse. During the Second Empire in France it adopted a Bonapartist stand.—11, 43

[^2]: Revue nationale—French Christian-democratic journal published by Philippe Bûchez and Jules Bastide in Paris from May 1847 to July 1848.—66

[^3]: Revue rétrospective ou Archives secrètes du dernier Gouvernement—French monthly published in Paris from 1833 to 1838; in 1848 appeared irregularly.—421

[^4]: Rheinische Zeitung für Politik, Handel und Gewerbe—German daily founded on January 1, 1842, as an organ of the oppositional circles of the Rhenish bourgeoisie, and published in Cologne till March 31, 1843; Marx was its editor from October 15, 1842, to March 17, 1843; under his influence the newspaper assumed a pronounced revolutionary-democratic character, which led to its suppression by the Government; Engels also contributed to it.— 527

[^5]: Der Satellit—supplement to the Kronstädter Zeitung (Transylvanian pro-Austrian newspaper) published in Kronstadt (Bra§ow).—453

[^6]: Schlesische Zeitung—German daily published in Breslau (Wroclaw) from 1742, organ of the constitutional-monarchist circles prior to and during the revolution of 1848-49.—391, 428

[^7]: Der Schweizer Bote—see Der aufrichtige und wohlerfahrene Schweizer Bote

[^8]: Schweizerische Bundeszeitung—see Berner Verfassungs-Freund



Schweizerische National-Zeitung—Swiss daily published in Basle from 1842.—42, 181

Der Schweizerischer Beobachter—Swiss liberal daily published in Basle from 1842; in 1848 its editor was Johann Karl Brenner.—42, 183

Schweizerischer Beobachter—Swiss newspaper published thrice weekly in Berne from 1833 to 1850.—183, 247

Schweizer Zeitung—see Der Freie Schweizer

Der Seeländer Anzeiger—Swiss weekly, organ of the petty-bourgeois socialists, published in Biel from 1837 to 1841 and in Berne from 1841 to 1852.—249, 250

Serbske Noviny—official organ of the Serbian Government published in Belgrade from 1835.—441 Siebenbürger Wochenblatt—weekly published in Kronstadt (Bragow).—454, 455

Slavenski jug—Croatian newspaper published in Agram (Zagreb) from 1848 to 1850.—410

Staats-Anzeiger—see Preussischer Staats-Anzeiger

Staats-Zeitung— see Preussischer Staats-Anzeiger

Südslavische Zeitung—Croatian newspaper, in 1849 organ of the Austro-Slav liberal- monarchist circles, published in German in Agram (Zagreb) from 1849 to 1852.— 347, 352

La Suisse—Swiss liberal newspaper published in Berne from 1846 to 1860.—58, 110, 179, 248

[^1]: Der Unabhängige—Swiss weekly published in Berne in 1848-49.—250

[^2]: Die Verbrüderung. Correspondenzblatt aller deutschen Arbeiter—workers' journal, organ of the Central Committee of the German Workers, published twice a week in Leipzig from October 1848 to June 1850; up to May 1849 its editor was Stephan Born.—505

[^3]: Verfassungs-Freund— see Berner Verfassungs-Freund

[^4]: Vossische Zeitung—see Königlich privilegirte Berlinische Zeitung von Staats- und gelehrten Sachen

[^5]: La vraie République. Journal quotidien, politique et littéraire—French political and literary daily, organ of the radical republicans; appeared under this title in Paris from March 26 until August 21, 1848, when it was banned. From March 29 to June 13, 1849, it bore the title Journal de la vraie République, its editorial board including Armand Barbes, Pierre Leroux and George Sand.—125

[^6]: Wächter—see Murter Wächter Wiener Zeitung—Austrian daily, official government newspaper, published in Vienna from 1780 to 1931. The Wiener Zeitung had several supplements, including

[^7]: Abend-Beilage zur Wiener Zeitung—290, 291, 300, 350, 351, 404, 415, 423, 432, 435, 437, 456, 458, 459, 479 Zeitung des Arbeiter-Vereines zu Köln—German newspaper published in April-October 1848, organ of the Cologne Workers' Association; until July 1848 it was edited by Andreas Gottschalk, and in July-September by Joseph Moll and Karl Schapper.— 189-90, 195

[^8]: Zürcher-Zeitung—Swiss liberal daily published in Zurich from 1780; it appeared under the title Neue Zürcher Zeitung until 1821, when it was renamed.—144
